    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_415939564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415939564" />
    <a title="Kala" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6551949-kala"><img alt="Kala" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320263692p2/6551949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415939564?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kala" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kala" href="/user/show/6551949-kala">Kala</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415939564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3334524650989906094">This review also posted on my blog at:<br/><a href='http://kalabookblog.blogspot.com/2012/09/stalk-me-by-jillian-dodd_16.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kala's Book Blog</a><br/><br/>I liked Jillian Dodd's book "That Boy" quite a bit. While I wasn't super pleased with the ending, I thought overall the writing was decent and the characters were likable.<br/><br/>I read the blurb for this book and thought that it sounded awesome. The book was supposed to be about popular girl Keatyn who has been living a sham life because she thought it was what she wanted (perfect friends, perfect boyfriend, etc), but it's all imploding around her a</span>
  <span id="freeText3334524650989906094" style="display:none">This review also posted on my blog at:<br><a href="http://kalabookblog.blogspot.com/2012/09/stalk-me-by-jillian-dodd_16.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Kala's Book Blog</a><br><br>I liked Jillian Dodd's book "That Boy" quite a bit. While I wasn't super pleased with the ending, I thought overall the writing was decent and the characters were likable.<br><br>I read the blurb for this book and thought that it sounded awesome. The book was supposed to be about popular girl Keatyn who has been living a sham life because she thought it was what she wanted (perfect friends, perfect boyfriend, etc), but it's all imploding around her and she starts to realize that the perfect life she thought she wanted might not be the best thing after all. <br><br>Yeah, that blurb is almost a complete fabrication. Well, I mean, it's kind of true for the first 15-20% of the book, but then the story changes drastically and none of that matters anymore.<br><br>Considering that I enjoyed That Boy, I figured I would like this one as well. <br><br>And I did!<br><br>For about 70-75% of the book. <br><br>Then the book died for me. It completely tanked. I struggled so hard to read the last quarter of this book because I was so pissed off at what happened and where Dodd was taking this story. I've since learned that she plans to make this a 6-book series and that disappoints me even more. For reasons I'll get in to later in this review, I'm possibly going to check out the sequels... but definitely not at $9.99 each for the ebooks. I was VERY happy I only paid $2.99 for this one.<br><br>There are some spoilers after this point, so BEWARE!<br><br>Stalk me starts off with Keatyn and her boyfriend Sander partying it up with her best friends Vanessa and RiAnne. And Cush, but I'll get in to him later. Sander keeps getting drunk at the parties all the time and won't have sex with her even though they've been dating a year. Vanessa is a really terrible friend and basically blackmails Keatyn into doing whatever she wants. RiAnne is basically Vanessa's lap dog.<br><br>Keatyn also apparently loves to surf and wakes up early to meet with her surfer friends, Damian and Brooklyn. She has a crush on Brooklyn and she doesn't know if it's requited. Even though Vanessa tells her not to, she breaks up with Sander. The breakup was actually well done and I really liked Sander. Unfortunately Sander disappears from the book after the breakup, despite Keatyn telling us he's her BFF and they have probably the most amicable breakup in history.<br><br>So Keatyn is single and starts hitting on Brooklyn. They make out one night and Keatyn thinks she's in love. Brooklyn doesn't call her for a few days and she gets all upset thinking she was just a hookup. After a few days he calls her and invites her to go away for the weekend with him and some friends to surf. She's all excited until he texts her and tells her he left early without her. She's emo about this and goes to a party with Cush.<br><br>Cush might be the absolute best character in this entire book. Cush is the cute, arrogant, adorable player who never dates, just has hookups, and has sexy dimples. He also is very good friends with Keatyn. They've been great friends for awhile - he goes dancing with her when her other friends wouldn't, she goes to awkward family functions with him as moral support, etc.<br><br>So, Keatyn is all upset that Brooklyn went off without her and she thinks he's a big player now. They get into a text fight where he tells her to grow up. That night she and Cush go to the party and end up kissing. She likes it a lot and Cush admits to her that he's been in love with her for awhile which is why he doesn't date girls. So Keatyn gives up her virginity and they start dating.<br><br>Every scene with Cush makes me feel like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391456ra/753858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cush is freaking awesome. They have an amazing time together until Keatyn is about to go on vacation and her BFF Vanessa sends her a cryptic text. Keatyn knows Vanessa is setting something up, so she stops by a party and finds another girl (Mandy) giving head to Cush. She's pissed off until she realizes Cush has been drugged. So Keatyn's best friend Vanessa sets this all up because she's a crazy stalker bitch. Keatyn takes Cush to a doctor and his parents find out and freak. For some really strange reason that I don't understand, except that the author needed to create a rift between them despite it not making any sense at all, Cush blames Keatyn for what happened and they break up. Don't ask, I don't understand why either.<br><br><br><br>So Keatyn leaves and ends up somehow starting up with Brooklyn again. They spend the summer having sex all over Europe and surfing. But Keatyn loves to dress up and go to clubs and dance, but Brooklyn hates it. He only likes her when she's playing beach bum without makeup. They argue about it and break up at her 17th birthday party. <br><br>At the same party, Cush and Keatyn make up and she tells him she loves him. Keatyn has realized that Cush loves all of her, not just pieces, and she wants to be with him. And from what I've seen so far, SHE IS RIGHT. They dance and make out and then Keatyn decides to go hang out with Brooklyn some more (WTF IS WRONG WITH YOU GIRL????).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391456ra/753859.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is where the book completely goes fucking nuts and starts sucking huge donkey balls.<br><br>While all this stuff is going on, Keatyn's mom (who is a famous actress) has been getting scary stalker letters. At Keatyn's 17th bday party, while she's hanging with Brooklyn, the stalker shows up and tries to abduct Keatyn. She gets away, but suddenly everything has to change.<br><br>Keatyn's mom decides Keatyn has to be sent to boarding school to be safe. She has to cut off all contact with all friends (except Brooklyn for some weird reason) and can't tell any of them that she's ok. Keatyn goes along with this after putting up very minimal resistance. She is vaguely upset about not seeing Cush anymore, but he's barely mentioned for the rest of the book. She professed her love for the guy and now she has to cut off all contact. He has no idea where she is. He has no idea why she refuses to talk to him. It's completely fucked up.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377720ra/733103.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Keatyn does't seem that upset. She gets emancipated from her parents and they open bank accounts for her because that way the stalker can't track her! She also changes her name to Keatyn Monroe, because that will hide her true identity! Her mom is a famous actress who is in a relationship with a famous actor. No matter what, Keatyn would occasionally be photographed by paparazzi. Her face is going to be known, especially by celebrity hounds who love to read entertainment magazines and blogs. She is also supposedly a dead ringer for her mother. But ... she will go to a boarding school full of rich people where no one will recognize her because it's important to the plot even though it MAKES NO FUCKING SENSE.<br><br>Oh, let's not forget that after professing her love to Cush, she fucks Brooklyn one last time before leaving for boarding school. Just because. It makes no sense why she can hang out with Brooklyn but not Cush, especially because the stalker knows Brooklyn, but whatever!<br><br>So....<br><br>Keatyn goes to boarding school, meets and starts making out with three different guys (Dallas, Riley, Aiden). <br><br>On her first night at boarding school she and Dallas get high and make out.<br><br>Second night, she purposely lets Riley into her room while she's wearing lingerie and a skimpy robe. <br><br>That same night, she holds hands with Aiden and this happens:<br><br><i><br>It takes everything I have to let go of his hand when I shake it.<br>My hand belongs in his.<br>Forever.<br>Don't laugh. I'm serious.<br>It belongs in his <b>forever</b><br></i><br><br>She has been at school all of TWO DAYS and like a week prior had confessed her love to Cush. Now she has completely forgotten about him and literally has so much chemistry with Aiden that she thinks her hand belongs in his FOREVER.<br><br>(sigh)<br><br>She also ends up on a ferris wheel with Aiden. And of course, when it's at the top, they kiss. It looks like this:<br><br><i><br>A slow, perfect, time-stood-still, fireworks-in-my-eyes kind of kiss.<br>And it was just a little kiss. No open mouths, no tongues; just a kiss.<br>A little teeny kiss.<br>Holy Shit.<br>I'm in love with him.<br></i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391413ra/753809.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yep, she was in love with Cush last week (and CUSH IS FUCKING AWESOME) and now she's in love with Aiden. Let's not forget that a week and a half ago she was in love with Brooklyn.<br><br>ANYWAYS.<br><br>The last lines of the book are:<br><br><i><br>All I have to say is: boarding school is no day at the beach.<br>It's way more exciting.<br></i><br><br>And to that, I say this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391456ra/753860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You create this fucking awesome character in Cush. His dialogue is awesome. His back story is awesome (what we get of it). EVERYTHING is fucking awesome about him. <br><br>You create this crazy dynamic between Keatyn and her "friends" at school, then fuck it all up by sending her to boarding school where we are now cut off completely from all the other characters you spend a few hundred pages getting us connected with and start us completely over in some shit boring boarding school with characters who are all cardboard cutouts of each other? <br><br>Am I supposed to give a fuck about Aiden or Dallas or Riley? I've known these characters for all of 30 seconds before Keatyn is forming these relationships with them that I don't give a fuck about because I WANT CUSH. Hell, I'll take Brooklyn, or Sander, or Vanessa. But giving me a fuck ton of new characters who all have the exact same personalities and making Keatyn get all in to them is basically a big FUCK YOU to the entire previous 80% of this book.<br><br>Ugh.<br><br>I originally rated this 2-stars, but after writing this I'm so pissed off at this story that I've had to drop it to 1-star. <br><br>Two things I also want to mention:<br><br>* Stalker plot is more like a minor sub-plot. However, that minor subplot fucked this entire story up by forcing the whole boarding school thing. <br>* This book suffers HUGELY from absent parent syndrome. Keatyn has no curfew and no rules. She regularly stays out entire nights. Her mom also encourages her to have sex and is super excited when Keatyn loses her virginity.<br><br><br>The ONLY reason that I would consider reading further into this series is if I read spoilers and find out Cush makes a comeback. Not that Keatyn deserves him, since she basically wants to run around fucking and kissing everyone, but he's the only character that makes this series redeemable. If book 2 is an Aiden/Keatyn love story I will pass. NOT INTERESTED.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3334524650989906094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8179357-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346526379p2/8179357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340678747?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/8179357-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8179357-lisa?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8179357-lisa?shelf=indie">indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340678747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13058383712207073533">4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Stalk Me was not quite what I expected but in a good way! It has the same great writing style Dodd showcased in That Boy and That Wedding but with a much edgier storyline that will appeal to mature young adults and adults. There are sooo many HOT, I mean HOT, boys in this book that I feel like I just got back from a trip to Swoonville and I will take that trip as many times as Jillian Dodd grants me a ticket!<br/><br/>Hot tamales! I am trying to think back to the last time I encountered a book wi</span>
  <span id="freeText13058383712207073533" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />Stalk Me was not quite what I expected but in a good way! It has the same great writing style Dodd showcased in That Boy and That Wedding but with a much edgier storyline that will appeal to mature young adults and adults. There are sooo many HOT, I mean HOT, boys in this book that I feel like I just got back from a trip to Swoonville and I will take that trip as many times as Jillian Dodd grants me a ticket!<br /><br />Hot tamales! I am trying to think back to the last time I encountered a book with soo many boys qualified for Swoonville residency and, well, I can’t think of one because I have not come across another book that took male hotness to THIS level. I usually have a clear favorite, you know, the guy I want the heroine to end up with and spend forever with. I did in this one too but then it changed and then it changed again and now I actually play for two teams…We will get to that later:)<br /><br />The story is fast paced and things are always changing and evolving. Ms. Dodd would give me a chair to sit in and I would be sitting pretty comfortably and then BAM, seat is taken from under me. I would then find another chair to sit in only to find myself on my rear end again! Stalk Me had me smiling, laughing, shedding tears and even left me breathless in a couple of scenes (thank to those teenage boys!).<br /><br />I had to remember that Keatyn is a teenage girl when reading this. She has the attention span of a teenage girl, the interests of a teenage girl and the standards of a teenage girl. As an adult, it was easy for me to say, did she really just do that?! But then I had to bring myself back to my teenage years and it all felt very real (besides the movie star parents and designer clothes). She has the emotions of a teenage girl; it is easy for her to cry, easy for her to get catty and easy for her to fall for a guy. I found her to also be very strong when I consider some of the things she has to go through during the book and she didn’t have the ultra whiny personality that some teenage girls have in YA books. I loved the way she was with her family; it showed her warm, caring side. She is popular but not too shallow. Overall, I found her to be a very likable girl!<br /><br />So this would be the part I would love to tell you about hero but that is a little difficult in this book so I am going to give you short impressions of “the boys” below.<br /><br />Sander – Oh My Gosh, these high school kids are kind of blind! I like you but I had your number from page 2 or 3. You are sweet, sexy and would make a great best friend. (Most of you will pick up on this too!)<br /><br />Brooklyn – I was hot and cold when it came to you. You were a little moody and I didn’t know what to make of you half the time. I don’t think you are “the one”.<br /><br />Daemon – I like Daemon and he is a great friend to Keatyn, I just haven’t seen enough of him to determine what I think about him yet. He is in a band and that always gets points with me.<br /><br />Cush - You may be a player but you can come play on my team whenever you want. He is super sweet and takes Keatyn for who she is and doesn’t try to change her. He also doesn’t care too much about being in the popular crowd and he seems to adore Keatyn. LOVES HIM!<br /><br />Riley and Dallas – I am still getting to know you and I think you could both be great friends with Keatyn. I think you are both witty and add some comic relief to this book!<br /><br />Aiden – I didn’t want anyone to come into Cush territory! I wanted all boys to STAY AWAY but you worked your way into my heart in the little bit of time that I have known you. Feel free to bring me a lunch anytime;)<br /><br />So right now, I am Team Cush and Team Aiden. My chemistry meteor was going wild when she was with both but I think it is anyones game at this point. I think I am leaning a little bit more toward Cush but with five more books to go, anything can happen! Oh, and there is always the possibility of more boys coming our way.<br /><br />I love a book that can keep me on my toes and I was definitely on my toes for most of this. There is so much I would like to say but I don’t want to ruin this for those who have not read it. I will say that it is one heck of a ride. I was actually kind of upset with Miss Dodd because of the situation Keatyn finds herself in about three-fourths of the way in but somehow, she completely swept me off my feet and made it alright. I cannot wait for Kiss Me in December. Can it just be December now??? I need to know where this is going!<br /><br />Team Cush Theme Song...<br /><br />Ah, Cush it – Cush it good<br />Ah, Cush it – Cush it real good<br />Ah, Cush it – Cush it good<br />Ah, Cush it – Cush it real good<br /><br />Hey! Ow!<br />Cush it Good!<br /><br />I have an interview with Jillian on my blog!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://lisasbookreview.wordpress.com/">http://lisasbookreview.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13058383712207073533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393829178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393829178" />
    <a title="Splage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4755656-splage"><img alt="Splage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371778615p2/4755656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393829178?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Splage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Splage" href="/user/show/4755656-splage">Splage</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393829178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17963849371091871923">Review posted to: <a href='http://sweptawaybyromance.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Swept Away By Romance</a><br/><b>4.5 Stars<br/>Genre: Contemporary, MATURE Young Adult Romance<br/>Heat Barometer: 3 out of 5 flames<br/>Written from the heroine’s, Keatyn, POV</b><br/><br/><b>Gossip Girl</b> meets <b>Mean Girls</b> with the setting in Malibu. I loved it and all its glamour, money, cars, killer clothes, popular crowd's antics and the fickleness of the teenage relationships-"in and out of love" before they could get their tongues out of each other's mouths. <br/><br/>This was a mature Young Adult romance because of the sexual</span>
  <span id="freeText17963849371091871923" style="display:none">Review posted to: <a href="http://sweptawaybyromance.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Swept Away By Romance</a><br /><b>4.5 Stars<br />Genre: Contemporary, MATURE Young Adult Romance<br />Heat Barometer: 3 out of 5 flames<br />Written from the heroine’s, Keatyn, POV</b><br /><br /><b>Gossip Girl</b> meets <b>Mean Girls</b> with the setting in Malibu. I loved it and all its glamour, money, cars, killer clothes, popular crowd's antics and the fickleness of the teenage relationships-"in and out of love" before they could get their tongues out of each other's mouths. <br /><br />This was a mature Young Adult romance because of the sexual situations and drugs. The sex wasn’t descriptive, but the wild parties seemed to make these kids much more advanced than 16 &amp; 17 years of age. At times I felt like I was watching an episode of The O.C. or the reality show Laguna Beach; fast kids with too much money and all the drama that goes with it…ADDICTIVE. Call me shallow, but I watched all of those night time soap operas faithfully and loved the teenage petty drama. I did keep thinking that all of these kids needed more parental supervision and guidance. Although Keatyn seemed very grounded and I loved her relationship with her movie star mother, step-father and 4 little sisters, she just had way too much freedom. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The older stalker guy was scaring me and creeping me out and I kept thinking if the parents just kept a little bit tighter rein on Keatyn this could all be prevented, but then the story wouldn’t have been as good. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am impressed by how much I like Jullian Dodd’s writing style, she has interesting stories that are current and just flow. They are so engaging and hip. She is on the cutting edge of fashion, the wardrobe descriptions alone are a good reason to read this book. The words and phrases she uses are cool and fresh, as well as, she is right there with all the pressures of today’s teens with sex, friendships, and drugs. What was really different with the romance in this book was that Keatyn was the heroine, but she had many different leading men (or boys) and the dynamic of her love life was forever changing. I was right there with her too. I would fall in love with one boy and then he would make a dumbass move and I was on to the next one. The book was populated with many hot guys to choose from and they all wanted Keatyn. I prefer to read one mature love story with big gestures, big love, hot sex and an overwhelming HEA. This is not that style, yet I devoured it and I couldn’t put it down. <br /><br />The book is named <b>Stalk Me</b>, but that seemed to be a smaller part of the story or it at least it took a backseat for me because I loved all the young relationship turmoil. I am sure the stalking issues will continue in the next book with a whole new cast of hot young guys, bitchy mean girls and high school situations. <br /><br /><b>Stalk Me (The Keatyn Chronicles)</b> is an on going series and Book 1 ends as a "to be continued" which bums me out because I want it NOW! Teaser chapters for book 2 look really good and I can't wait to read it in December. I believe there is going to be 6 books in the series, not sure I have the patience to have mine and Keatyn's heart shattered over and over through six books, but I am going to step out of my comfort zone and try to enjoy every moment of this teenager’s life. <b>Stalk Me</b> was absolutely a brilliant start!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17963849371091871923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_816063535" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="SimplyƝì₭" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20178587-simply"><img alt="SimplyƝì₭" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552929015p2/20178587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816063535?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SimplyƝì₭" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SimplyƝì₭" href="/user/show/20178587-simply">SimplyƝì₭</a>
      </span>

<div id="review_412110997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412110997" />
    <a title="Megan11" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3956866-megan11"><img alt="Megan11" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308940700p2/3956866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412110997?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan11" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan11" href="/user/show/3956866-megan11">Megan11</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412110997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16347055220344826430">Honestly, I wanted to like this book, and give it 2.5 stars, I just couldn't bring myself to do it. This book is completely unrealistic, the main character is so superficial, indecisive, morally corrupt and obnoxious. I found myself in the beginning thinking one thing, and then getting excited thinking she is finally going to wisen up, then being pissed off, because really she is just another stuck up, backstabbing, skanky highschool idiot. I really thought she was going to have some type of tur</span>
  <span id="freeText16347055220344826430" style="display:none">Honestly, I wanted to like this book, and give it 2.5 stars, I just couldn't bring myself to do it. This book is completely unrealistic, the main character is so superficial, indecisive, morally corrupt and obnoxious. I found myself in the beginning thinking one thing, and then getting excited thinking she is finally going to wisen up, then being pissed off, because really she is just another stuck up, backstabbing, skanky highschool idiot. I really thought she was going to have some type of turn around, realize her ways and start over as a better person at her new school, well I was wrong, and she did not learn a damn thing. I do not even knopw what to say about the guys, ofcourse they are all good looking, swoon worthy, typical guys, but how many of them do we really need to have?? All these guys really basically say is, you are so hot, blah blah, I love you, let's have sex, aaaaand that's kind of it. The writer is clever in making you think these guys are of some different variety, deep and caring and outsiders, but it just makes them look that much more like a bunch of douchebags, because they really are no different than any other guy, just wrappoed in a more attractive package. I found her "parents" to be a pathetic example for anyone to follow, but I am sure that is how it really is out in Malibu, which is pretty scary. The whole stalker thing is pretty anticlimactic and seemed like a filler really in a story mainly about a girl who wants to have sex and makes every possible stupid choice given, while whining about everything. If I read the next book, it will only be because I feel like I need her to redeem herself somewhat, with Aiden, or on her own, something..but if the next one is just some more misadventures of a horny teenager, I will probably throw the book against a wall. I usually don't review that many books because who the hell really wants my opinion, but this book just irked me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16347055220344826430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6962487069177158588">If you want a light read, try this!<br/><br/>This book has the ingredients for an exciting next read: <b>catchy title</b>, <b>totally hot, swoon-worthy boys</b> and a <b>filthy, rich heroine</b> who seriously needs to make up her mind.<br/><br/><i>TEAM CUSH all the way!!!</i><br/><br/>Halfway through the novel, I kept thinking, Keatyn can't keep bouncing from one guy to another. It was a frustrating read for me.<br/><br/>Even before everything was spelled out for the heroine, I already knew two things. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ That Sander was gay and Brooklyn did not rea</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6962487069177158588" style="display:none">If you want a light read, try this!<br /><br />This book has the ingredients for an exciting next read: <b>catchy title</b>, <b>totally hot, swoon-worthy boys</b> and a <b>filthy, rich heroine</b> who seriously needs to make up her mind.<br /><br /><i>TEAM CUSH all the way!!!</i><br /><br />Halfway through the novel, I kept thinking, Keatyn can't keep bouncing from one guy to another. It was a frustrating read for me.<br /><br />Even before everything was spelled out for the heroine, I already knew two things. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ That Sander was gay and Brooklyn did not really love her THAT MUCH. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The moment I realized these things, I just want to shout at Keatyn, <i>Get a freaking clue already!</i> Let me tell you, she's THAT clueless most of the time.<br /><br />I know that I wasn't being patient but you could just imagine my frustration when I realized that it's already past 3/4 of the novel, and she's making out with new hotties and I'm like, <i>who do you really end up with, Keatyn, huh</i>?<br /><br />Then it's the end. I was like, WHAT?? Did this book just kept me hanging? I didn't know this was the first in a six book series until I've read the acknowledgements. No warnings whatsoever.<br /><br />So consider yourself forewarned, I repeat, <b>this book is the first in a SIX book series</b>.<br /><br />Don't expect any HEA yet. Because I did, and look what happened to me. I was totally frustrated.<br /><br />But no matter how many hotties appear til book 6, I'll stay loyal to the Cushman!<br /><br />Anyway, I liked Jillian Dodd's writing. Fun and easy to read.<br /><br />UPDATED:<br />I was using mobile app for Goodreads so imagine my surprise when I opened the GR desktop site, and saw the book title with (The Keatyn Chronicles #1) next to it. Maybe, GR mobile app should show not just the book title but also the series name. Just saying.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492592210?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessa Russo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessa Russo" href="/user/show/6371633-jessa-russo">Jessa Russo</a>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6371633-jessa-russo?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6371633-jessa-russo?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492592210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17154030522273882873">FIRST OF ALL, this book is NOT YOUNG ADULT. Though the main character acts like a very immature 14yo at best, her REACTIONS to sexual activities are FAR from what is realistic in YA. <br/><br/>There is a fine line between girls exploring their sexuality in YA books, or even being completely promiscuous and confident sexually, and girls acting out of character for their age. The sexual situations in STALK ME were what I imagine the author dreams about, NOT what any teen girl actually experiences. There wer</span>
  <span id="freeText17154030522273882873" style="display:none">FIRST OF ALL, this book is NOT YOUNG ADULT. Though the main character acts like a very immature 14yo at best, her REACTIONS to sexual activities are FAR from what is realistic in YA. <br /><br />There is a fine line between girls exploring their sexuality in YA books, or even being completely promiscuous and confident sexually, and girls acting out of character for their age. The sexual situations in STALK ME were what I imagine the author dreams about, NOT what any teen girl actually experiences. There were none of the insecurities or awkwardness that come with discovering your sexuality, or being intimate with boys for the first time. Keatyn handled each situation like a PRO, and I had a very hard time believing anything in this book. <br /><br />UPDATE 4/28: I rarely leave a book unfinished, so I forced myself to finish this one in hopes that the only likable character would win in the end. Poor Cush.<br /><br />I'm sorry, but I can't rate this book. PLEASE do not let your young adult daughters read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17154030522273882873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_416866650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416866650" />
    <a title="Atmika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2651380-atmika"><img alt="Atmika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591916344p2/2651380.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416866650?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Atmika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Atmika" href="/user/show/2651380-atmika">Atmika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416866650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9229887786476170452">When I started the book I thought that I would like it. It seemed cute and fun. It started well and I was okay when we had only three guys(I think!) in the picture. <br/><br/>I liked Cush the most. He was super cute and adorable, but for no rhyme or reason he does something that is completely unlike his character and royally screws up. So, Keatyn breaks up with him and the book starts to go downhill from here. <br/><br/>The MC Keatyn is shallow and jumps from one guy to next and apparently she loves all of them. hu</span>
  <span id="freeText9229887786476170452" style="display:none">When I started the book I thought that I would like it. It seemed cute and fun. It started well and I was okay when we had only three guys(I think!) in the picture. <br><br>I liked Cush the most. He was super cute and adorable, but for no rhyme or reason he does something that is completely unlike his character and royally screws up. So, Keatyn breaks up with him and the book starts to go downhill from here. <br><br>The MC Keatyn is shallow and jumps from one guy to next and apparently she loves all of them. huh! I just don't understand her. I don't have a problem with her being spoiled or fickle minded or stupid. My problem is that the character shows no growth. She has no redeeming qualities and is so damn irritating. <br><br>The ENDING is my biggest issue. End the book when the stalker gets caught, don't just drag the story because there is a sequel planned. I don't want her to go to a boarding school and meet more guys. (NO!!!) And poor Cush, he was just put out of the picture. Why? If Brooklyn can know about Keatyn's location, why can't Cush? <br><br>There are many loose ends and so many things that make no sense. <br>The book has no logic and kinda assumes that readers are STUPID. I don't like that. I won't pick up the second book. <br><br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-IeDOeR9--M0/UKv8GH_AzrI/AAAAAAAABVY/9O9cWXt3g7M/s1600/tumblr_mcd2adrlcI1r67g8ro1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="141" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391601ra/754121.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
<br><br>The book could have been loads better. Many people do like it so, read more reviews, think about it and then decide whether you want to buy it or not. My suggestion is to save your money and avoid this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9229887786476170452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hgMePhNRVHSyQ/XOs1f9leV6XVy3GJK46z/BqadcbFwBtiPAgKNDGPc5R3toPgHGW0KM2PQYQi9r2MVrqZyU1Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hwACaX1w22IjILqQJjMKzoDo5lX/VQR++xtZomhpWNgAtT+X7oLMDmZaCCX9WvadPtA30bxV1Ol7/F1gZqmgUQ==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText1598332468607220855" style="display:none">Jillian is a <i>USA TODAY</i> bestselling author who writes fun romance novels with characters her readers fall in love with--from the boy next door in the That Boy trilogy, to the daughter of a famous actress in The Keatyn Chronicles®, to a kick-ass young assassin in the Spy Girl® series. Jillian's books have enthralled more than two million readers since she burst onto the indie scene in 2011.<br /><br />She lives in a small Florida beach town, is married to her college sweetheart, has two grown children, and two Labrador Retrievers named Cali and Camber. When she's not working, she likes to travel, paint, shop for shoes, watch football, and go to the beach.<br /><br />Check out Jillian’s website for added content: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jilliandodd.net">www.jilliandodd.net</a><br /><br /></span>

While romance abounds in the roles he plays, he’s convinced he’ll never find his own happily ever after—until he meets a woman who just might change that. \n\nShelby Benson — The beautiful cocktail waitress and wanna-be actress struggles to make ends meet. A chance encounter with Riley Johnson is her lucky break and the golden ticket to everything she’s ever dreamed of—fame, power, money, sex, and love.\n\nWritten soap-opera style with multiple points
